<a href="#ntc190-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0190"
id="ntr190-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0190">(<span
class="super">190</span>)</a>  The Court has not yet ruled on this
question in relation to the UCTD but it has been asked to provide
interpretation in Case C-829/18 <span class="italic">Crédit
Logement</span> (pending on 31 May 2019). One element is that it is
difficult for consumers to prove the absence of such information.
Furthermore, EU directives providing for specific pre-contractual
information obligations confirm that this obligation lies with the
trader, e.g. Articles 5 and 6 of Directive 2011/83/EU on consumer rights
([OJ L 304, 22.11.2011, p.
64](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2011:304:TOC)),
Articles 5 and 6 of Directive 2008/48/EC on credit agreements for
consumers ([OJ L 133, 22.5.2008, p.
66](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2008:133:TOC)),
Article 14 of Directive 2014/17/EU on credit agreements for consumers
relating to residential immovable property ([OJ L 60, 28.2.2014, p.
34](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2014:060:TOC)) or
Article 5 of Directive (EU) 2015/2302 ([OJ L 326, 11.12.2015, p.
1](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2015:326:TOC)) on
package travel and linked travel arrangements. Some of them have also
codified the principle that the burden of proof in this respect is on
the trader, for instance, in Article 6(9) of Directive 2011/83/EU and
Article 8 of Directive (EU) 2015/2302.

id="ntr191-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0191">(<span
class="super">191</span>)</a>  Case C-472/10
<span class="italic">Invitel</span>; Case C-92/11
<span class="italic">RWE Vertrieb</span>; Case C-143/13
<span class="italic">Matei and Matei</span>.

<a href="#ntc199-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0199"
id="ntr199-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0199">(<span
class="super">199</span>)</a>  [OJ L 293, 31.10.2008, p.
3](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2008:293:TOC). Under
this Regulation, air fares/rates available to the general public shall
include the applicable conditions. The final price shall at all times be
indicated and shall include the applicable air fare/rate as well as all
applicable taxes, and charges, surcharges and fees which are unavoidable
and foreseeable at the time of publication. In addition, at least the
air fare/rate, taxes, airport charges and other charges, surcharges or
fees, such as those related to security or fuel must be specified.

<a href="#ntc209-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0209"
id="ntr209-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0209">(<span
class="super">209</span>)</a>  Case C-448/17 <span class="italic">EOS
KSI Slovensko</span>, paragraph 66 and point 3 of the operative part.
The Court considered that the provision only of a mathematical formula
for the calculation of the APR without the information necessary to
calculate the APR is equivalent to failing to provide the APR.

<a href="#ntc210-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0210"
id="ntr210-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0210">(<span
class="super">210</span>)</a>  Pursuant to Article 43 of Directive
2014/17/EU ([OJ L 60, 28.2.2014, p.
34](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2014:060:TOC)), this
Directive shall not apply to credit agreements existing before 21 March
2016.

<a href="#ntc211-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0211"
id="ntr211-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0211">(<span
class="super">211</span>)</a>  Case C-92/11 <span class="italic">RWE
Vertrieb</span>. See in particular point 2 of the operative part:
‘Articles 3 and 5 of Directive 93/13 in conjunction with Article 3(3) of
Directive 2003/55/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26
June 2003 concerning common rules for the internal market in natural gas
and repealing Directive 98/30/EC must be interpreted as meaning that, in
order to assess whether a standard contractual term by which a supply
undertaking reserves the right to vary the charge for the supply of gas
complies with the requirements of good faith, balance and transparency
laid down by those directives, it is of fundamental importance:

|  |  |
|----|----|
| — | whether the contract sets out in transparent fashion the reason for and method of the variation of those charges, so that the consumer can foresee, on the basis of clear, intelligible criteria, the alterations that may be made to those charges. The lack of information on the point before the contract is concluded cannot, in principle, be compensated for by the mere fact that consumers will, during the performance of the contract, be informed in good time of a variation of the charges and of their right to terminate the contract if they do not wish to accept the variation; and |

|  |  |
|----|----|
| — | whether the right of termination conferred on the consumer can actually be exercised in the specific circumstances. \[…\]’ |

<a href="#ntc212-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0212"
id="ntr212-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0212">(<span
class="super">212</span>)</a>  In Joined Cases C-359/11 and C-400/11
<span class="italic">Schulz and Egbringhoff</span>, the Court ruled on
transparency requirements adjusting contract for the supply of
electricity and gas covered by universal supply obligation. The Court
held that national legislation which determines the content of this type
of consumer contracts and allows the price of that supply to be
adjusted, but which does not ensure that customers are to be given
adequate notice, before that adjustment comes into effect, of the
reasons and preconditions for the adjustment, as well as its scope, is
against the transparency provisions of Directive 2003/54/EC of the
European Parliament and of the Council of 26 June 2003 concerning common
rules for the internal market in electricity and repealing Directive
96/92/EC — Statements made with regard to decommissioning and waste
management activities ([OJ L 176, 15.7.2003, p.
37](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2003:176:TOC)) and
Directive 2003/55/EC ([OJ L 176, 15.7.2003, p.
57](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2003:176:TOC)),
replaced by Directive 2009/72/EC ([OJ L 211, 14.8.2009, p.
55](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2009:211:TOC)) and
Directive 2009/73/EC ([OJ L 211, 14.8.2009, p.
94](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2009:211:TOC))
respectively. The content of the contracts at issue being determined by
German legislative provisions that are mandatory, the UCTD was not
applicable.

<a href="#ntc213-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0213"
id="ntr213-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0213">(<span
class="super">213</span>)</a>  Case C-421/14 <span class="italic">Banco
Primus</span>, paragraph 60. See also Case C-186/16
<span class="italic">Andriciuc</span>, paragraph 57.

<a href="#ntc214-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0214"
id="ntr214-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0214">(<span
class="super">214</span>)</a>  Reference to Case C-415/11
<span class="italic">Aziz</span>, paragraph 69.

<a href="#ntc215-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0215"
id="ntr215-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0215">(<span
class="super">215</span>)</a>  In his conclusions of 21 March 2019 in
Case C-34/18 <span class="italic">Ottília Lovasné Tóth</span>,
paragraphs 56-62, Advocate General Hogan even suggests that the absence
of good faith is not a separate condition for the unfairness of a
contract term at all, although some statements of the Court (e.g. in
Case C-186/16 <span class="italic">Andriciuc</span>, paragraph 56:
‘\[…\] it is for the referring to assess \[…\] first, the possible
failure to observe the requirement of good faith and second, the
existence of a significant imbalance within the meaning of Article 3(1)
of Directive 93/13.’) do not necessarily support this position.

<a href="#ntc216-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0216"
id="ntr216-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0216">(<span
class="super">216</span>)</a>  See Section 3.4.2.

<a href="#ntc217-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0217"
id="ntr217-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0217">(<span
class="super">217</span>)</a>  The Court reminded the national courts of
this provision in several rulings, e.g. Case C-226/12
<span class="italic">Constructora Principado</span>, the second indent
of the operative part and paragraph 30; Case C-415/11
<span class="italic">Aziz</span>, paragraph 71; Case C-243/08
<span class="italic">Pannon GSM</span>, paragraph 39; Case C-137/08
<span class="italic">VB Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraph 42; Case
C-421/14 <span class="italic">Banco Primus</span>, paragraph 61; Case
C-186/16 <span class="italic">Andriciuc</span>, paragraph 53. Case
C-421/14 <span class="italic">Banco Primus</span>, paragraph 61, first
sentence reads as follows: ‘In addition, pursuant to Article 4(1) of the
directive, the unfairness of a contractual term must be assessed taking
into account the nature of the goods or services for which the contract
was concluded and by referring, at the time of conclusion of the
contract, to all of the circumstances attending its conclusion’.

<a href="#ntc218-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0218"
id="ntr218-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0218">(<span
class="super">218</span>)</a>  For instance, where the national
transposition of Article 3(1) does not require the absence of good faith
or that the imbalance has to be ‘significant’. See also Section 2.1 on
minimum harmonisation.

<a href="#ntc219-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0219"
id="ntr219-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0219">(<span
class="super">219</span>)</a>  See also Section 3.4.7 on the role of the
Annex.

<a href="#ntc220-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0220"
id="ntr220-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0220">(<span
class="super">220</span>)</a>  Case C-472/10
<span class="italic">Invitel</span>, paragraphs 25 and 26; Case C-243/08
<span class="italic">Pannon GSM</span>, paragraphs 37 and 38; Case

<a href="#ntc250-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0250"
id="ntr250-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0250">(<span
class="super">250</span>)</a>  Although, in line with the principle of
minimum harmonisation, national law may provide that lack of
transparency can have this immediate consequence. See Section 2 on the
relationship of the UCTD with national law and § 307 (1) of the German
Civil Code (BGB).

<a href="#ntc251-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0251"
id="ntr251-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0251">(<span
class="super">251</span>)</a>  See Section 3.2.1.

<a href="#ntc252-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0252"
id="ntr252-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0252">(<span
class="super">252</span>)</a>  This is confirmed implicit or explicitly
in several rulings, for instance in Cases C-421/14
<span class="italic">Banco Primus</span>, paragraphs 62-67, in
particular in paragraph 64 and the second indent of paragraph 67, Case
C-119/17 — <span class="italic">Lupean</span>, paragraphs 22-31, or
C-118/17 <span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraph 49.

<a href="#ntc253-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0253"
id="ntr253-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0253">(<span
class="super">253</span>)</a>  Lack of transparency is not mentioned as
a condition in Article 3(1). This is different only for contract terms
defining the main-subject matter or whose assessment would require an
examination of the adequacy of the price or remuneration.

<a href="#ntc254-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0254"
id="ntr254-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0254">(<span
class="super">254</span>)</a>  Confirmed in Case C-342/13
<span class="italic">Katalin Sebestyén</span>, paragraph 34: ‘However,
even assuming that the general information the consumer receives before
concluding a contract satisfies the requirement under Article 5 that it
be plain and intelligible, that fact alone cannot rule out the
unfairness of a clause \[…\].’

<a href="#ntc255-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0255"
id="ntr255-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0255">(<span
class="super">255</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-472/10
<span class="italic">Invitel</span>, paragraph 28 and end of point 1 of
the operative part.: ‘It is for the national court, \[…\], to assess,
with regard to Article 3(1) and (3) of Council Directive 93/13/EEC of 5
April 1993 on unfair terms in consumer contracts, the unfair nature of a
term included in the general business conditions of consumer contracts
by which a seller or supplier provides for a unilateral amendment of
fees connected with the service to be provided, without setting out
clearly the method of fixing those fees or specifying a valid reason for
that amendment. As part of this assessment, the national court must
determine, inter alia, whether, in light of all the terms appearing in
the general business conditions of consumer contracts which include the
contested term, and in the light of the national legislation setting out
rights and obligations which could supplement those provided by the
general business conditions at issue, the reasons for, or the method of,
the amendment of the fees connected with the service to be provided are
set out in plain, intelligible language and, as the case may be, whether
consumers have a right to terminate the contract.’

Case C-92/11 <span class="italic">RWE Vertrieb</span>, point 2 of the
operative part: ‘Articles 3 and 5 of Directive 93/13 in conjunction with
Article 3(3) of Directive 2003/55/EC \[…\] must be interpreted as
meaning that, in order to assess whether a standard contractual term by
which a supply undertaking reserves the right to vary the charge for the
supply of gas complies with the requirements of good faith, balance and
transparency laid down by those directives, it is of fundamental
importance:

|  |  |
|----|----|
| — | whether the contract sets out in transparent fashion the reason for and method of the variation of those charges, so that the consumer can foresee, on the basis of clear, intelligible criteria, the alterations that may be made to those charges. \[…\]; and |

|  |  |
|----|----|
| — | whether the right of termination conferred on the consumer can actually be exercised in the specific circumstances. |

It is for the national court to carry out that assessment with regard to
all the circumstances of the particular case, including all the general
terms and conditions of the consumer contracts of which the term at
issue forms part.’

<a href="#ntc256-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0256"
id="ntr256-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0256">(<span
class="super">256</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-191/15
<span class="italic">Verein für Konsumenteninformation v Amazon</span>,
paragraph 65: ‘It is for the national court to determine whether, having
regard to the particular circumstances of the case, a term meets the
requirements of good faith, balance and transparency.’ See also Joined
Cases C-70/17 and C-179/17 <span class="italic">Abanca Corporación
Bancaria and Bankia</span>, paragraph 50 and Case C-26/13
<span class="italic">Kásler and Káslerné Rábai</span>, paragraph 40.

Case C-92/11 <span class="italic">RWE Vertrieb</span>, paragraph 47: ‘A
standard term which allows such a unilateral adjustment must, however,
meet the requirements of good faith, balance and transparency laid down
by those directives.’

<a href="#ntc257-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0257"
id="ntr257-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0257">(<span
class="super">257</span>)</a>  Case C-472/10

für Konsumenteninformation v Amazon</span>, paragraph 68, an extract of
which is quoted here. The preceding paragraph 67 reads: ‘In those
circumstances, \[…\], a pre-formulated term on the choice of the
applicable law designating the law of the Member State in which the
seller or supplier is established is unfair only in so far as it
displays certain specific characteristics inherent in its wording or
context which cause a significant imbalance in the rights and
obligations of the parties.’

that there is a (rebuttable) legal presumption that specific types of
contract terms are unfair.

<a href="#ntc274-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0274"
id="ntr274-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0274">(<span
class="super">274</span>)</a>  In particular, paragraphs 59 and 74;
Paragraph 74 reads as follows: ‘It follows, in particular from Articles
3 and 5 of Directive 93/13 and Paragraph 1(j) and (l) and Paragraph 2(b)
and (d) of the annex to that directive that it is of fundamental
importance, for the purpose of complying with the requirement of
transparency, to determine whether the loan agreement sets out
transparently the reasons for and the particularities of the mechanism
for altering the interest rate and the relationship between that
mechanism and the other terms relating to the lender's remuneration, so
that the consumer can foresee, on the basis of clear, intelligible
criteria, the economic consequences for him which derive from it.’

<a href="#ntc275-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0275"
id="ntr275-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0275">(<span
class="super">275</span>)</a>

<div>

‘terms which have the object or effect of “excluding or hindering the
consumer's right to take legal action or exercise any other legal
remedy, particularly by requiring the consumer to take disputes
exclusively to arbitration not covered by legal provisions, unduly
restricting the evidence available to him or imposing on him a burden of
proof which, according to the applicable law, should lie with another
party to the contract”’.

<a href="#ntc284-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0284"
id="ntr284-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0284">(<span
class="super">284</span>)</a>  The Court has, however, clarified that,
in court proceedings, after being informed about the unfairness of a
contract term, consumers may decide not to rely on this protection (See
Sections 4.3.3, as well as 5.5.1 and 5.5.5). In Case C-452/18
<span class="italic">Ibercaja</span> (pending on 31 May 2019) the Court
is called to consider contract terms contained in a novation agreement
according to which a consumer waived the right to make restitution
claims based on contract terms that may have been unfair in connection
with a ‘settlement’ concerning the consequences of an unfair contract
term and may give further guidance on this principle.

<a href="#ntc285-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0285"
id="ntr285-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0285">(<span
class="super">285</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-154/15, C-307/15 and
C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutiérrez Naranjo,</span> paragraph 61.

<a href="#ntc286-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0286"
id="ntr286-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0286">(<span
class="super">286</span>)</a>  Case C-243/08 <span class="italic">Pannon
GSM</span>, paragraph 28 quoted here.

<a href="#ntc287-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0287"
id="ntr287-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0287">(<span
class="super">287</span>)</a>  The fact that also consumers will
generally be subject to time-limits for using remedies in ongoing
proceedings or may be subject to reasonable limitation periods when
claiming the restitution of payments made on the basis of unfair
contract terms is a different matter, see Joined Cases C-154/15,
C-307/15 and C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutierrez Naranjo</span>,
paragraphs 69-70.

<a href="#ntc288-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0288"
id="ntr288-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0288">(<span
class="super">288</span>)</a>  Case C-473/00
<span class="italic">Cofidis</span>, paragraph 38. The obligation of
national courts to assess the unfairness of contract terms of their own
motion (<span class="italic">ex officio</span>) is discussed in Section
5.

<a href="#ntc289-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0289"
id="ntr289-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0289">(<span
class="super">289</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-154/15, C-307/15 and
C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutiérrez Naranjo</span>, operative part
and paragraphs 73-75.

<a href="#ntc290-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0290"
id="ntr290-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0290">(<span
class="super">290</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-96/16 and C-94/17
<span class="italic">Banco Santander Escobedo Cortés</span>, paragraph
73. In Case C-618/10 <span class="italic">Banco Español de
Crédito</span>, the Court established the fundamental principles
concerning the consequences to be drawn from the non-binding character
of unfair contract terms. They have been confirmed in numerous cases,
e.g. Case C-488/11 <span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse</span>; Case
C-26/13 <span class="italic">Kásler and Káslerné Rábai</span>; Joined
Cases C-482/13, C-484/13, C-485/13 and C-487/13
<span class="italic">Unicaja Banco y Caixabank</span>; Case C-421/14
<span class="italic">Banco Primus,</span> paragraph 71; and Joined Cases
C-154/15, C-307/15 and C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutierrez
Naranjo,</span> paragraphs 57-61.

<a href="#ntc291-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0291"
id="ntr291-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0291">(<span
class="super">291</span>)</a>  Reference to Case C-421/14
<span class="italic">Banco Primus,</span> paragraph 71 and the case-law
cited.

<a href="#ntc292-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0292"
id="ntr292-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0292">(<span
class="super">292</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-488/11
<span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse</span>, paragraph 59: ‘\[…\] Article
6(1) of the directive cannot be interpreted as allowing the national
court, in the case where it establishes that a penalty clause in a
contract concluded between a seller or supplier and a consumer is
unfair, to reduce the amount of the penalty imposed on the consumer
instead of excluding the application of that clause in its entirety
\[…\].’

<a href="#ntc293-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0293"
id="ntr293-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0293">(<span
class="super">293</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-154/15, C-307/15 and
C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutierrez Naranjo</span>, paragraphs 60
and 62.

<a href="#ntc294-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0294"
id="ntr294-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0294">(<span
class="super">294</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-488/11
<span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse</span>, paragraph 58: ‘The Court has
also observed that that interpretation is, moreover, borne out by the
objective and overall scheme of the directive. In this connection, it
has pointed out that, given the nature and significance of the public
interest which constitutes the basis of the protection guaranteed to
consumers, the directive requires Member States, as is apparent from
Article 7(1) thereof, to provide for adequate and effective means “to
prevent the continued use of unfair terms in contracts concluded with
consumers by sellers or suppliers”. If it were open to the national
court to revise the content of unfair terms included in such contracts,
such a power would be liable to compromise attainment of the long-term
objective of Article 7 of the directive, since it would weaken the
dissuasive effect on sellers or suppliers of the straightforward
non-application of those unfair terms with regard to the consumer
(<span class="italic">Banco Español de Crédito</span>, paragraphs 66 to
69).’

<a href="#ntc295-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0295"
id="ntr295-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0295">(<span
class="super">295</span>)</a>  The Court confirmed this in Joined Case
C-70/17 and C-179/17 <span class="italic">Abanca Corporación Bancaria
and Bankia</span>, paragraph 55: ‘In the present case, the mere removal
of the ground for termination making the terms at issue in the main
proceedings unfair would ultimately be tantamount to revising the
content of those terms by altering their substance. Therefore, those
terms cannot be maintained in part without directly adversely affecting
the dissuasive effect referred to in the preceding paragraph.’

<a href="#ntc296-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0296"
id="ntr296-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0296">(<span
class="super">296</span>)</a>  Case C-26/13 <span class="italic">Kásler
and Káslerné Rábai</span> and Case C-186/16
<span class="italic">Andriciuc</span> in connection with Article 4 (2).

<a href="#ntc297-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0297"
id="ntr297-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0297">(<span
class="super">297</span>)</a>  Case C-472/11
<span class="italic">Invitel</span> and Case C-92/11
<span class="italic">RWE Vertrieb.</span>

<a href="#ntc298-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0298"
id="ntr298-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0298">(<span
class="super">298</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-96/16 and C-94/17
<span class="italic">Banco Santander Escobedo Cortes</span>, in
particular paragraphs 76 and 77.

<a href="#ntc299-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0299"
id="ntr299-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0299">(<span
class="super">299</span>)</a>  In Joined Case C-70/17 and C-179/17
<span class="italic">Abanca Corporación Bancaria and Bankia</span>, the
Court did not directly comment on this question although, in Case
C-70/17, the Spanish Supreme Court had specifically referred to this
doctrine.

<a href="#ntc300-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0300"
id="ntr300-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0300">(<span
class="super">300</span>)</a>  Also referred to as ‘geltungserhaltende
Reduktion’ in German doctrine and jurisprudence.

<a href="#ntc304-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0304"

class="super">304</span>)</a>  In Case C-618/10
<span class="italic">Banco Español de Crédito</span>, paragraph 65, and
Case C-488/11 <span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse</span>, paragraph 57
the CJEU stated that ‘\[the\] contract must continue in existence, in
principle, without any amendment other than that resulting from the
deletion of the unfair terms, in so far as, in accordance with the rules
of domestic law, such continuity of the contract is
<span class="bold">legally</span> possible.’

<a href="#ntc313-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0313"
id="ntr313-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0313">(<span
class="super">313</span>)</a>  The Court confirmed the principles
established in Case C-26/13 <span class="italic">Kásler and Káslerné
Rábai</span>, paragraph 85, in Joined Cases C-482/13, C-484/13, C-485/13
and C-487/13 <span class="italic">Unicaja Banco y Caixabank</span>,
paragraph 33, and in Joined Cases C-96/16 and C-94/17
<span class="italic">Banco Santander Escobedo Cortés,</span> paragraph
74 and Joined Case C-70/17 and C-179/17 <span class="italic">Abanca
Corporación Bancaria and Bankia</span>, paragraphs 56-63.

<a href="#ntc314-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0314"
id="ntr314-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0314">(<span
class="super">314</span>)</a>  The Court emphasised the condition that
the consequences must be ‘particularly negative’ for consumers so that
the latter would be ‘penalised’ in Cases C-118/17
<span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraph 54, C-96/16 and C-94/17
<span class="italic">Banco Santander and Escobedo Cortés</span>,
paragraph 74, C-51/17 <span class="italic">OTP Bank and OTP
Faktoring</span>, paragraph 61 or that it is ‘contrary to the interests’
of the consumer, <span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraph 55.

<a href="#ntc315-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0315"
id="ntr315-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0315">(<span
class="super">315</span>)</a>  Joined Case C-70/17 and C-179/17
<span class="italic">Abanca Corporación Bancaria and Bankia</span>,

<a href="#ntc316-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0316"
id="ntr316-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0316">(<span
class="super">316</span>)</a>  Case C-26/13 <span class="italic">Kásler
and Káslerné Rábai</span>, paragraphs 80-81; Case C-92/11
<span class="italic">RWE Vertrieb</span>, paragraph 26; Case C-280/13
<span class="italic">Barclays Bank</span>, paragraphs 31 and 42; Case
C-7/16 <span class="italic">Banco Popular Español and PL
Salvador</span>, paragraph 21; Case C-446/17
<span class="italic">Woonhaven Antwerpen BV CVBA v Berkani and
Hajji</span>, paragraph 25.

<a href="#ntc317-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0317"
id="ntr317-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0317">(<span
class="super">317</span>)</a>  Case C-260/18
<span class="italic">Dziubak</span> (pending on 31 May 2019). This case
concerns, amongst other questions, the consequences to be drawn from the
potential nullity of a contract term setting out the currency conversion
mechanism for a loan denominated in a foreign currency.

<a href="#ntc318-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0318"
id="ntr318-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0318">(<span
class="super">318</span>)</a>  In his opinion of 14 May 2019 in Case
C-260/18 <span class="italic">Dziubak</span>, Advocate General
Pitruzzella, considers that the notion of supplementary provision has to
be interpreted narrowly in the sense that it only applies to provisions
which can as such replace the unfair contract term, without requiring
‘creativity’ by the judge, given that such ‘creativity’ would, in his
view, correspond to a revision of unfair contract terms (paragraphs
77-79).

<a href="#ntc319-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0319"
id="ntr319-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0319">(<span
class="super">319</span>)</a>  Joined Case C-70/17 and C-179/17
<span class="italic">Abanca Corporación Bancaria and Bankia</span>,
paragraph 59.

<a href="#ntc320-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0320"
id="ntr320-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0320">(<span
class="super">320</span>)</a>  Case C-126/18 <span class="italic">Gómez
del Moral Guasch</span> (pending on 31 May 2019), which involves the
potential nullity of the reference in a mortgage credit contract to an
index for the applicable interest rate. If this contract term were to be
unfair, there would be no agreement on the applicable interest rate.

<a href="#ntc321-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0321"
id="ntr321-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0321">(<span
class="super">321</span>)</a>  Opinion of Advocate General Pitruzzella
of 14 May 2019 in Case C-260/18 <span class="italic">Dziubak</span>,
paragraph 60. This is to be distinguished from the assessment of the
unfairness of the contract term under Article 3(1), which takes into
account the circumstances at the conclusion of the contract.

<a href="#ntc322-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0322"
id="ntr322-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0322">(<span
class="super">322</span>)</a>  Case C-118/17
<span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraph 55.

<a href="#ntc323-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0323"
id="ntr323-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0323">(<span
class="super">323</span>)</a>  Case C-118/17
<span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraphs 51-55.

<a href="#ntc324-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0324"
id="ntr324-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0324">(<span
class="super">324</span>)</a>  In Case C-118/17
<span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraphs 53-55, the consumer's
interest in the nullity of the contract seemed to coincide with
consumer's request. In his opinion of 14 May 2019 in Case C-260/18
<span class="italic">Dziubak</span>, paragraph 67, Advocate General
Pitruzzella considers the consumer's preference to be decisive. In
Joined Cases C-70/17 and C-179/17 <span class="italic">Abanca
Corporación Bancaria</span>, paragraphs 61 and 62, the Court refers to
an assessment to be carried out by the national judge, in light of the
applicable national law, but does not exclude that the national judge
raises this question with the consumer.

<a href="#ntc325-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0325"
id="ntr325-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0325">(<span
class="super">325</span>)</a>  See Section 4.3.3 below.

<a href="#ntc342-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0342"

<a href="#ntc348-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0348"
id="ntr348-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0348">(<span
class="super">348</span>)</a>  The Court applies
<span class="italic">effectiveness</span> of the protection under the
UCTD as a standard for the assessment of procedural constraints as well
a positive requirement underlying, in particular,
<span class="italic">ex officio</span> control, e.g. Case C-176/17
<span class="italic">Profi Credit Polska</span>, paragraph 44; Case
C-49/14 <span class="italic">Finanmadrid</span>, paragraph 4. See also
Case C-497/13 <span class="italic">Froukje Faber</span>, paragraphs
42-47 concerning Directive 1999/44/EC on certain aspects of the sale of
consumer goods and associated guarantees ([OJ L 171, 7.7.1999, p.
12](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:1999:171:TOC)).

<a href="#ntc377-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0377"
id="ntr377-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0377">(<span
class="super">377</span>)</a>  More detailed implications of the
<span class="italic">ex officio</span> principle are presented in the
sub-sections below.

<a href="#ntc378-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0378"
id="ntr378-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0378">(<span
class="super">378</span>)</a>  Case C-243/08 <span class="italic">Pannon
GSM,</span> operative part. Under earlier case law, starting in Joined
Cases C-240/98-244/98 <span class="italic">Océano Grupo Editorial</span>
and confirmed in several subsequent rulings, the Court required that
national courts had to have <span class="italic">the power</span> to
examine unfair contract terms of their own motion. This development in
the case law of the Court is explained in Case C-168/15
<span class="italic">Milena Tomášová</span>, paragraphs 28-31.

<a href="#ntc379-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0379"
id="ntr379-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0379">(<span
class="super">379</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-421/14
<span class="italic">Banco Primus</span>, paragraph 43, quoted here.

<a href="#ntc380-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0380"
id="ntr380-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0380">(<span
class="super">380</span>)</a>  References to Cases
<span class="italic">C-415/11 Aziz,</span> paragraph 46 and the case law
cited, and C-154/15, C-307/15 and C-308/15
<span class="italic">Gutiérrez Naranjo and Others,</span> paragraph 58.

<a href="#ntc381-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0381"
id="ntr381-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0381">(<span
class="super">381</span>)</a>  Case C-168/05
<span class="italic">Mostaza Claro</span>, paragraphs 27 and 28; Case
C-473/00 <span class="italic">Cofidis</span>, paragraph 32; Case
C-240/98 <span class="italic">Océano Grupo Editorial,</span> paragraph
28.

id="ntr382-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0382">(<span
class="super">382</span>)</a>  Case C-397/11 <span class="italic">Erika
Jöros</span>, paragraphs 30, 35 and 36.

<a href="#ntc383-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0383"
id="ntr383-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0383">(<span
class="super">383</span>)</a>  An overview of the guiding principles in
the Member States, including implications for consumer cases, can be
found in Chapter 3 of the Evaluation study of national procedural laws
and practices in terms of their impact on the free circulation of
national procedural laws and practices in terms of their impact on the
free circulation of judgments and on the equivalence and effectiveness
of the procedural protection of consumers under EU consumer law,
JUST/2014/RCON/PR/CIVI/0082 — Strand 2 Procedural Protection of
Consumers.

<a href="#ntc384-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0384"
id="ntr384-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0384">(<span
class="super">384</span>)</a>  See also Case C-497/13
<span class="italic">Froukje Faber</span>, paragraph 38.

<a href="#ntc385-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0385"
id="ntr385-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0385">(<span
class="super">385</span>)</a>  A more active role of judges may also
depend also on factors such as whether one party is identified as the
weaker party, e.g. a consumer, or on whether a party is represented, in
particular by a lawyer.

<a href="#ntc386-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0386"
id="ntr386-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0386">(<span
class="super">386</span>)</a>  C-40/08 <span class="italic">Asturcom
Telecomunicaciones</span>, paragraph 47. See also Case C-137/08
<span class="italic">VB Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraph 56; Case
C-415/11 <span class="italic">Aziz</span>, paragraph 47; Case C-472/11
<span class="italic">Banif Plus Bank</span>, paragraph 24.

<a href="#ntc387-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0387"
id="ntr387-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0387">(<span
class="super">387</span>)</a>  C-40/08 <span class="italic">Asturcom
Telecomunicaciones</span>, paragraphs 41-46. In the case at issue the
consumer had neither participated in the arbitration proceedings
initiated against her by the trader nor brought an action for annulment
of the arbitration award within two months. However, in this case, the
Court considered that there was an obligation for the national courts to
assess the compliance of the arbitration award with the UCTD based on
the equivalence principle.

<a href="#ntc388-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0388"
id="ntr388-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0388">(<span
class="super">388</span>)</a>  Case C-32/14 <span class="italic">ERSTE
Bank Hungary</span>, paragraph 63.

<a href="#ntc389-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0389"
id="ntr389-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0389">(<span
class="super">389</span>)</a>  The ex officio obligations based on the
equivalence principle are explained, for instance, in Joined Cases
C-430/93 and C-431/93 <span class="italic">van Schijndel and van
Veen</span>, paragraphs 13 and 14, with reference to previous case law:

|  |  |
|----|----|
| ‘13 | Where, by virtue of domestic law, courts or tribunals must raise of their own motion points of law based on binding domestic rules which have not been raised by the parties, such an obligation also exists where binding Community rules are concerned (see, in particular, the judgment in Case 33/76 <span class="italic">Rewe v Landwirtschaftskammer für das Saarland</span>, paragraph 5). |

|  |  |
|----|----|
| 14 | The position is the same if domestic law confers on courts and tribunals a discretion to apply of their own motion binding rules of law. Indeed, pursuant to the principle of cooperation laid down in Article 5 of the Treaty, it is for national courts to ensure the legal protection which persons derive from the direct effect of provisions of Community law (see, in particular, the judgment in Case C-213/89 <span class="italic">Factortame and Others</span>, paragraph 19).’ |

<a href="#ntc390-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0390"
id="ntr390-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0390">(<span
class="super">390</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-488/11
<span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse,</span> paragraphs 44-46, quoted
here. In this ruling the Court also referred to Cases C-40/08
<span class="italic">Asturcom Telecomunicaciones</span>, paragraphs 52
and 54, C-76/10 <span class="italic">Pohotovost'</span>, paragraph 5.

id="ntr391-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0391">(<span

<span class="italic">PKO</span>, paragraph 49. All those cases concerned

<span class="italic">Banco Español de Crédito</span>.

class="super">409</span>)</a>  Case C-421/14 <span class="italic">Banco
Primus</span>, point 2 of the operative part and paragraph 52. While
this case relates to mortgage enforcement, the same logic must apply to
other types of procedures. The assessment of rules on
<span class="italic">res judicata</span> under the effectiveness
principles, including with regard to <span class="italic">ex
officio</span> control is discussed specifically under point 5.4.2,
where inter alia paragraph 52 of <span class="italic">Banco
Primus</span> is quoted.

<a href="#ntc419-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0419"
id="ntr419-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0419">(<span
class="super">419</span>)</a>  Case C-632/17
<span class="italic">PKO</span>, paragraph 45.

<a href="#ntc420-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0420"
id="ntr420-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0420">(<span
class="super">420</span>)</a>  [OJ L 351, 20.12.2012, p.
1](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2012:351:TOC); the
Regulation has repealed Council Regulation (EC) No 44/2001 ([OJ L 12,
16.1.2001, p.
1](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2001:012:TOC)).

<a href="#ntc421-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0421"
id="ntr421-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0421">(<span
class="super">421</span>)</a>  Pursuant to Article 17(3) of Regulation
(EU) No 1215/2012 ([OJ L 351, 20.12.2012, p.
1](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2012:351:TOC)), these
rules are not applicable to contracts of transport other than contracts
which, for an inclusive price, provide for a combination of travel and
accommodation. Moreover, Articles 19 and 25 of Regulation (EU) No
1215/2012 allow the parties to a contract to derogate in certain cases
from the rules on jurisdiction. The Court has been requested to provide
interpretation in this respect in Case C-629/18 <span class="italic">EN,
FM, GL v Ryanair</span> (pending on 31 May 2019).

<a href="#ntc422-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0422"
id="ntr422-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0422">(<span
class="super">422</span>)</a>  For instance, by giving a seller or
supplier the option of suing a consumer in a court other than a court of
their place of residence.

<a href="#ntc423-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0423"
id="ntr423-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0423">(<span
class="super">423</span>)</a>  In Joined Cases C-240/98 to C-244/98
<span class="italic">Océano Grupo Editorial,</span> paragraph 21 the
Court considered that such jurisdiction arrangements in non-negotiated
contract terms satisfy all the criteria to be classed as unfair for the
purposes of the UCTD.

<a href="#ntc449-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0449"
id="ntr449-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0449">(<span
class="super">449</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-537/12 and C-116/13
<span class="italic">Banco Popular Español and Banco de Valencia,</span>
paragraph 60; and Case C-169/14, <span class="italic">Sánchez Morcillo
and Abril Garcia,</span> paragraph 28.

<a href="#ntc450-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0450"
id="ntr450-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0450">(<span
class="super">450</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-568/14 to C-570/14
<span class="italic">Ismael Fernández Oliva.</span> This case concerned
the possibility of obtaining interim relief individual proceedings while
a collective legal action is pending.

<a href="#ntc451-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0451"
id="ntr451-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0451">(<span
class="super">451</span>)</a>  The Court established this requirement in
connection with reimbursement claims based on the unfairness of contract
terms and parallel collective legal proceedings which lead to the
suspension of the individual action. Joined Case C-568/14 to C-570/14
<span class="italic">Ismael Fernández Oliva</span>, paragraphs 32–37.
The significant risk was based on the fact that, in view of the conduct
and complexities of the national procedure the consumers may have been
unaware of their rights or may not have appreciated their extent. As it
reflects a general principle, this requirement would appear to reply
also in other procedural situations.

<a href="#ntc452-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0452"
id="ntr452-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0452">(<span
class="super">452</span>)</a>  Case C-618/10 <span class="italic">Banco
Español de Crédito</span>, paragraph 54.

<a href="#ntc453-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0453"
id="ntr453-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0453">(<span
class="super">453</span>)</a>  This follows already from the formula
through which the Court defines the presence of a significant risk.
Furthermore, the fact that unawareness or lack of appreciation of the
extent of consumer or procedural rights can in itself justify
<span class="italic">ex officio</span> intervention. The Court confirmed
this in Joined Cases C-568/14 to C-570/14 <span class="italic">Ismael
Fernández Oliva</span>, paragraph 33, when it stated that ‘\[…\], in
view of the conduct and complexities of the national procedure in
question in the main proceedings, \[…\], there is a not insignificant
risk that the consumer concerned may not make such an application, even
though the substantive conditions required under national law for the
grant of interim relief may be satisfied, because he is unaware of or
does not appreciate the extent of his rights.’

<a href="#ntc454-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0454"
id="ntr454-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0454">(<span
class="super">454</span>)</a>  Case C-8/14
<span class="italic">BBVA</span>, paragraphs 36-40.

<a href="#ntc455-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0455"
id="ntr455-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0455">(<span
class="super">455</span>)</a>  The Court considered a rather specific
situation in Case C-8/14 <span class="italic">BBVA</span>, paragraphs
33-42.

<a href="#ntc456-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0456"
id="ntr456-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0456">(<span
class="super">456</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-154/15, C-307/15 and

class="super">471</span>)</a>  Case C-243/08 <span class="italic">Pannon
GSM</span>, point 2 of the operative part.

<a href="#ntc472-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0472"
id="ntr472-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0472">(<span
class="super">472</span>)</a>  Reference to Case C-397/11
<span class="italic">Erika Jőrös,</span> C-397/11, paragraph 42.

<a href="#ntc473-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0473"
id="ntr473-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0473">(<span
class="super">473</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-154/15, C-307/15 and
C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutierrez Naranjo</span>, paragraph 59.

<a href="#ntc474-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0474"
id="ntr474-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0474">(<span
class="super">474</span>)</a>  See Joined Cases C-568/14 to C-570/14
<span class="italic">Ismael Fernández Oliva.</span>

<a href="#ntc475-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0475"
id="ntr475-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0475">(<span
class="super">475</span>)</a>  This is important with regard to
consumers as well as sellers and suppliers, as follows for instance from
Cases C-243/08 <span class="italic">Pannon GSM</span>, C-472/11
<span class="italic">Banif Plus Bank</span>, paragraphs 29-35, C-488/11
<span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse</span>, paragraph 52 and C-119/15
<span class="italic">Biuro podróży ‘Partner’</span>, paragraphs 22-47.
See also Section 5.5.4.

<a href="#ntc476-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0476"
id="ntr476-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0476">(<span
class="super">476</span>)</a>  Case C-137/08 <span class="italic">VB
Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraph 49 and the subsequent paragraphs.

Regarding the substantive criteria to be taken into account please see
Section 3.

<a href="#ntc477-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0477"
id="ntr477-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0477">(<span
class="super">477</span>)</a>  Case C-137/08 <span class="italic">VB
Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraphs 49-51. For questions relating to the
scope of the UCTD, see Section 1.2.

<a href="#ntc478-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0478"
id="ntr478-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0478">(<span
class="super">478</span>)</a>  Case C-497/13
<span class="italic">Froukje Faber</span>, point one of the operative
part and paragraphs 46-48. This ruling concerns Directive 1999/44/EC
([OJ L 171, 7.7.1999, p.
12](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:1999:171:TOC)), but
applies <span class="italic">mutatis mutandis</span> to the UCTD.
Furthermore, in order to establish whether the terms in question falls
within the scope of the UCTD, courts inevitably have to investigate
whether there is a contract between a seller or supplier or a consumer.

<a href="#ntc479-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0479"
id="ntr479-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0479">(<span
class="super">479</span>)</a>  Case C-137/08 <span class="italic">VB
Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraphs 49-51. Courts have to take into
account that Article 3(2) UCTD contains a specific rule on the burden of
proof regarding the question of whether a pre-formulated contract term
was negotiated individually or not.

<a href="#ntc480-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0480"
id="ntr480-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0480">(<span
class="super">480</span>)</a>  E.g. Case C-176/17
<span class="italic">Profi Credit Polska,</span> paragraph 42: ‘Against
that background, it should, in the first place, be pointed out that,
whilst, in accordance with settled case-law, a national court is bound
to assess of its own motion whether a contractual term falling within
the scope of Directive 93/13 is unfair and by so doing to compensate for
the imbalance existing between the consumer and the seller or supplier,
that is so only if the national court has available to it the legal and
factual elements necessary for that task’. In this paragraph the Court
refers to Cases C-377/14 <span class="italic">Radlinger and
Radlingerová</span>, paragraph 52 and the case-law cited there, and
C-154/15, C-307/15 and C-308/15 <span class="italic">Gutiérrez Naranjo
and Others</span>, paragraph 58.

<a href="#ntc481-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0481"
id="ntr481-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0481">(<span
class="super">481</span>)</a>  Case C-497/13
<span class="italic">Froukje Faber</span>, point one of the operative
part and paragraphs 46-48, Case C-137/08 <span class="italic">VB
Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, point 3 of the operative part and paragraphs
45-51.

<a href="#ntc482-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0482"
id="ntr482-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0482">(<span
class="super">482</span>)</a>  The Court used this term in Case C-137/08
<span class="italic">VB Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraph 56 and
confirmed it in Case C-472/11 paragraph 24 which is quoted here.

<a href="#ntc483-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0483"
id="ntr483-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0483">(<span
class="super">483</span>)</a>  References to Cases C-137/08
<span class="italic">VB Pénzügyi Lízing</span>, paragraph 56, and
C-618/10 <span class="italic">Banco Español de Crédito,</span> paragraph
44.

<a href="#ntc484-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0484"
id="ntr484-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0484">(<span
class="super">484</span>)</a>  Case C-497/13
<span class="italic">Froukje Faber</span> in particular, paragraphs 44
and 46. The quotation is from paragraph 46. Although this case concerned
Directive 1999/44/EC ([OJ L 171, 7.7.1999, p.
12](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:1999:171:TOC)), it
addresses a horizontal question of consumer contract law and is
applicable <span class="italic">mutatis mutandis</span> to the status of
consumer under the UCTD.

<a href="#ntc485-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0485"
id="ntr485-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0485">(<span
class="super">485</span>)</a>  In this connection they have to take into
account the provisions on the burden of proof in Article 3(2). See
Section 1.2.2.1. If in a given Member State also individually negotiated
contract terms are subject to the provisions transposing the UCTD, this
assessment is, of course, not necessary.

<a href="#ntc486-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0486"
id="ntr486-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0486">(<span
class="super">486</span>)</a>  Section 3.3.1, Case C-186/16
<span class="italic">Andriciuc</span>, paragraph 43, Case C-119/17
<span class="italic">Lupean</span>, paragraph 23.

<a href="#ntc487-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0487"
id="ntr487-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0487">(<span
class="super">487</span>)</a>  Case C-618/10 <span class="italic">Banco
Español de Crédito.</span>

<a href="#ntc488-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0488"
id="ntr488-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0488">(<span
class="super">488</span>)</a>  Case C-176/17 <span class="italic">Profi
Credit Polska</span> and Case C-632/17 <span class="italic">PKO.</span>

<a href="#ntc489-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0489"
id="ntr489-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0489">(<span
class="super">489</span>)</a>  Case C-632/17
<span class="italic">PKO</span>, paragraph 38: ‘\[…\], in circumstances
such as those at issue in the main proceedings, a national court is not
in a position to examine whether a contractual term is unfair so long as
it does not have available to it all the factual and legal elements for
that purpose’. The Court refers to the same finding in Case C-176/17
<span class="italic">Profi Credit Polska,</span> paragraph 47.

<a href="#ntc490-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0490"
id="ntr490-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0490">(<span
class="super">490</span>)</a>  Cases C-618/10 <span class="italic">Banco
Español de Crédito</span>, paragraph 57, C-49/14
<span class="italic">Finanmadrid</span>, paragraph 36; C-32/14
<span class="italic">ERSTE Bank Hungary</span>, paragraph 43. In other
cases, for instance in Case C-488/11 <span class="italic">Asbeek
Brusse</span>, paragraph 40, the Court used the formulation
‘<span class="italic">as soon as</span> it has available the necessary
factual and legal elements’.

<a href="#ntc491-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0491"
id="ntr491-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0491">(<span
class="super">491</span>)</a>  Case C-176/17 <span class="italic">Profi
Credit Polska</span> and Case C-632/17 <span class="italic">PKO.</span>

<a href="#ntc492-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0492"
id="ntr492-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0492">(<span
class="super">492</span>)</a>  Case C-176/17 <span class="italic">Profi
Credit Polska</span>, paragraphs 69 and 70; Case C-632/17
<span class="italic">PKO</span>, paragraphs 45-49.

<a href="#ntc493-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0493"
id="ntr493-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0493">(<span
class="super">493</span>)</a>  Case C-632/17
<span class="italic">PKO</span>, paragraphs 37 and 38; Case C-176/17
<span class="italic">Profi Credit Polska</span>, paragraph 47.

<a href="#ntc494-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0494"
id="ntr494-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0494">(<span
class="super">494</span>)</a>  Case C-632/17
<span class="italic">PKO</span>, paragraph 49, which is quoted here and
which contains a reference to the previous ruling in Case C-176/17
<span class="italic">Profi Credit Polska</span>, paragraph 71.

<a href="#ntc495-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0495"
id="ntr495-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0495">(<span
class="super">495</span>)</a>  Case C-472/11 <span class="italic">Banif
Plus Bank</span>, paragraphs 29-35, Case C-488/11
<span class="italic">Asbeek Brusse</span>, paragraph 52: ‘\[…\], it must
be recalled that the principle of <span class="italic">audi alteram
partem</span>, as a general rule, requires the national court which has
found of its own motion that a contractual term is unfair to inform the
parties to the dispute of that fact and to invite each of them to set
out its views on that matter, with the opportunity to challenge the
views of the other party, in accordance with the formal requirements
laid down in that regard by the national rules of procedure
(<span class="italic">Banif Plus Bank</span>, paragraphs 31 and 36)’.

<a href="#ntc496-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0496"
id="ntr496-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0496">(<span
class="super">496</span>)</a>  Case C-243/08 <span class="italic">Pannon
GSM</span>. See also Case C-488/11 <span class="italic">Asbeek
Brusse</span>, paragraph 49, Case C-618/10 <span class="italic">Banco
Español de Crédito</span>, paragraph 63, and Case C-472/11
<span class="italic">Banif Plus Bank</span>, paragraph 27, Joined Cases
C-70/17 and C-179/17 <span class="italic">Abanca Corporación Bancaria
and Bankia</span>, paragraph 63.

<a href="#ntc497-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0497"
id="ntr497-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0497">(<span
class="super">497</span>)</a>  This is a general principle of EU law
which the Court reiterated, for instance, in Case C-397/11
<span class="italic">Erika Jörös</span>, paragraph 32.

<a href="#ntc498-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0498"
id="ntr498-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0498">(<span
class="super">498</span>)</a>  See Sections 2.2 and 5.2 as well as Case
C-118/17 <span class="italic">Dunai</span>, paragraph 61.

<a href="#ntc499-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0499"
id="ntr499-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0499">(<span
class="super">499</span>)</a>  Section 5.3.1.

<a href="#ntc500-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0500"
id="ntr500-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0500">(<span
class="super">500</span>)</a>  Case C-168/15 <span class="italic">Milena
Tomášová.</span>

<a href="#ntc501-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0501"
id="ntr501-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0501">(<span
class="super">501</span>)</a>  Case C-125/04
<span class="italic">Denuit</span>. See also Case Case C-503/15
<span class="italic">Margarit Panicello</span> in relation to the
procedure before a <span class="italic">Secretario Judicial</span>
(Registrar) regarding an action for the recovery of lawyers'fees.

<a href="#ntc502-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0502"
id="ntr502-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0502">(<span
class="super">502</span>)</a>  Case C-32/14 <span class="italic">ERSTE
Bank Hungary</span>, paragraphs 47-49.

<a href="#ntc503-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0503"
id="ntr503-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0503">(<span
class="super">503</span>)</a>  Case C-32/14 <span class="italic">ERSTE
Bank Hungary</span>, paragraphs 55-58.

<a href="#ntc504-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0504"
id="ntr504-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0504">(<span
class="super">504</span>)</a>  This follows, for instance from Case
C-32/14 <span class="italic">ERSTE Bank Hungary</span>, in particular
paragraph 59, and Case C-448/17 <span class="italic">EOS KSI
Slovensko</span>, paragraphs 44-54.

<a href="#ntc505-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0505"
id="ntr505-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0505">(<span
class="super">505</span>)</a>  Case C-40/08
<span class="italic">Asturcom Telecomunicaciones</span>, Case C-76/10
<span class="italic">Pohotovost'.</span>

<a href="#ntc506-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0506"
id="ntr506-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0506">(<span
class="super">506</span>)</a>  To see whether consumers are effectively
protected, one would have to look at the guarantees during the entire
procedure, including the requirements for the agreement to submit a
dispute to arbitration, the procedural guarantees in the arbitration
proceedings, the risk of consumers' not using remedies against an
arbitration award because of their limited knowledge and information, as
well the guarantees at the judicial stage, including
<span class="italic">ex officio</span> assessment of unfair contract
terms.

<a href="#ntc507-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0507"
id="ntr507-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0507">(<span
class="super">507</span>)</a>  This follows from the rulings on the UCTD
in relation to Articles 6(1), 7(1) and the principle
<span class="italic">effectiveness</span>. Furthermore, the Court's
ruling in Joined Cases C-317/08, C-318/08, C319/08 and C-320/08
<span class="italic">Alassini</span>, which relates to Directive
2002/22/EC (Universal Service Directive) ([OJ L 108, 24.4.2002, p.
51](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2002:108:TOC)),
expresses the general principle that national laws on settlement
procedures may not prevent effective judicial protection of consumers
and end users (See, in particular, the operative part and paragraphs 49,
53, 54, 58, 61, 62 and 65).

<a href="#ntc508-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0508"
id="ntr508-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0508">(<span
class="super">508</span>)</a>  See point 1(q) of the Annex to the UCTD
and Case C-342/13 <span class="italic">Katalin Sebestyén</span>,
paragraph 36. Insofar as national law prohibits arbitration proceedings
against consumers, such clauses will be invalid already under the
relevant national provisions.

<a href="#ntc509-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0509"
id="ntr509-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0509">(<span
class="super">509</span>)</a>  Article 10 of Directive 2013/11/EU of the
European Parliament and of the Council of 21 May 2013 on alternative
dispute resolution for consumer disputes and amending Regulation (EC) No
2006/2004 and Directive 2009/22/EC (Directive on consumer ADR) ([OJ L
165, 18.6.2013, p.
63](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2013:165:TOC)): ‘an
agreement between a consumer and a trader to submit complaints to an ADR
entity is not binding on the consumer if it was concluded before the
dispute has materialised and if it has the effect of depriving the
consumer of his right to bring an action before the courts for the
settlement of the dispute.’

<a href="#ntc510-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0510"
id="ntr510-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0510">(<span
class="super">510</span>)</a>  Directive 2009/22/EC of the European
Parliament and of the Council of 23 April 2009 on injunctions for the
protection of consumers' interests ([OJ L 110, 1.5.2009, p.
30](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2009:110:TOC)).

<a href="#ntc511-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0511"
id="ntr511-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0511">(<span
class="super">511</span>)</a>  Case C-472/10
<span class="italic">Invitel</span>, paragraph 35.

<a href="#ntc512-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0512"
id="ntr512-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0512">(<span
class="super">512</span>)</a>  Case C-372/99
<span class="italic">Commission</span> v
<span class="italic">Italy</span>, paragraph 15.

<a href="#ntc513-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0513"
id="ntr513-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0513">(<span

<a href="#ntc515-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0515"

<span class="italic">Invitel</span>, paragraphs 43 and 44.

<a href="#ntc517-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0517"
id="ntr517-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0517">(<span
class="super">517</span>)</a>  Case C-119/15 <span class="italic">Biuro
podróży ‘Partner’</span>, paragraphs 22-47.

<a href="#ntc518-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0518"

<span class="italic">Sales Sinués and Drame Ba</span>, paragraph 30.

<a href="#ntc519-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0519"

class="super">519</span>)</a>  Opinion of Advocate General Szpunar in

<a href="#ntc520-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0520"

class="super">520</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-381/14 and C-385/14

<a href="#ntc521-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0521"
id="ntr521-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0521">(<span
class="super">521</span>)</a>  Joined Cases C-568/14 to C-570/14
<span class="italic">Ismael Fernández Oliva</span>. See also Section
5.3.2.

<a href="#ntc522-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0522"
id="ntr522-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0522">(<span
class="super">522</span>)</a>  Case C-413/12
<span class="italic">Asociación de Consumidores Independientes de
Castilla y León</span>, paragraphs 49-53.

<a href="#ntc523-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0523"
id="ntr523-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0523">(<span
class="super">523</span>)</a>  Under that provision, the courts of the
Member State where the defendant is established or has its address have
jurisdiction to hear actions for an injunction brought by consumer
protection associations from other Member States.

<a href="#ntc524-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0524"
id="ntr524-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0524">(<span
class="super">524</span>)</a>  Case C-167/00
<span class="italic">Henkel</span>, paragraph 50 as regards Article 5(3)
of the Convention of 27 September 1968 on Jurisdiction and the
Enforcement of Judgments in Civil and Commercial Matters (Brussels
Convention).

<a href="#ntc525-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0525"
id="ntr525-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0525">(<span
class="super">525</span>)</a>  Council Regulation (EC) No 44/2001 of 22
December 2000 on jurisdiction and the recognition and enforcement of
judgments in civil and commercial matters ([OJ L 12, 16.1.2001, p.
1](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2001:012:TOC)), that
was repealed and replaced by Regulation (EU) No 1215/2012 of the
European Parliament and of the Council ([OJ L 351, 20.12.2012, p.
1](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2012:351:TOC)); see
Case C-548/12 <span class="italic">Brogsitter</span>, paragraph 19; Case
C-191/15 <span class="italic">Verein für Konsumenteninformation v
Amazon</span>, paragraph 38.

<a href="#ntc526-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0526"
id="ntr526-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0526">(<span
class="super">526</span>)</a>  Case C-167/00
<span class="italic">Henkel</span>, paragraph 42.

<a href="#ntc527-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0527"
id="ntr527-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0527">(<span
class="super">527</span>)</a>  Regulation (EC) No 864/2007 of the
European Parliament and of the Council of 11 July 2007 on the law
applicable to non-contractual obligations (Rome II) ([OJ L 199,
31.7.2007, p.
40](./../../../../legal-content/EN/AUTO/?uri=OJ:L:2007:199:TOC)).

<a href="#ntc528-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0528"
id="ntr528-C_2019323EN.01000401-E0528">(<span
class="super">528</span>)</a>  Regulation (EC) No 593/2008 ([OJ L 177,
4.7.2008, p.

<tr class="table">

<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>Directive 87/102/EEC — Consumer

<div id="C_2019323EN.01009001">

<div>

ANNEX II

Overview of notifications under Article 8a
UCTD <a href="#ntr1-C_2019323EN.01009001-E0001"
id="ntc1-C_2019323EN.01009001-E0001">(<span
class="super note-tag">1</span>)</a>

This table reflects information which the Member States have notified to
the Commission under Article 8a of Directive 93/13/EEC (UCTD). It does
not represent a complete overview of the national transposition measures
for Directives 93/13/EEC and can provide only a rough indication of some
particularities of the relevant national law. For instance, depending on
the precise formulation in the relevant national provisions, a ‘grey
list’ can have different legal implications.

This information is also accessible on the following website, which will
be updated regularly:

https://ec.europa.eu/info/notifications-under-article-8a-directive-93-13-eec_en

<table class="table" width="100%" data-border="0" data-cellspacing="0"
data-cellpadding="0">
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 39%" />
<col style="width: 61%" />
</colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>BELGIUM</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
standard contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a
black list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>BULGARIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
standard contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a
black list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>CZECHIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law also covers the
unfairness of individually negotiated contract terms, and contains a
list of contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a
black list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>DENMARK</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law does not go beyond
the minimum standard of the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>GERMANY</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains two black
lists of standard contract terms considered unfair.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>ESTONIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
standard contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a
black list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>IRELAND</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law does not go beyond
the minimum standard of the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>GREECE</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
standard contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a
black list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>SPAIN</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law has broadened the
scope of the unfairness assessment to contract terms relating to the
definition of the main subject matter of the contract and to the
adequacy of the price or remuneration, regardless of whether such terms
are in plain, intelligible language.</p>
<p>National law also contains lists of terms considered unfair in all
circumstances (i.e. black lists).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>FRANCE</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law also covers the
unfairness of individually negotiated contract terms and contains a list
of terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a black list) and
a list of terms considered unfair unless it is proven that they are fair
(i.e. a form of grey list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>CROATIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law does not go beyond
the minimum standard of the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>ITALY</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a black
list), including where such terms have been negotiated individually, and
a list of contract terms which are presumed to be unfair in the absence
of proof to the contrary (i.e. a form of grey list). The list has been
extended compared to the Annex to the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>CYPRUS</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law does not go beyond
the minimum standard of the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>LATVIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law does not go beyond
the minimum standard of the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>LITHUANIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains no
provisions going beyond the minimum standard of the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>LUXEMBURG</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law has broadened the
scope of the unfairness assessment to individually negotiated contract
terms and to the main subject matter.</p>
<p>National law contains a black list of contractual terms which are
considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a black list) which has
been extended compared to the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>HUNGARY</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. a black list) and a
list of terms considered unfair until the contrary in proven (i.e. a
form of grey list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>MALTA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law has broadened the
scope of the unfairness assessment to individually negotiated contract
terms and to the adequacy of the price or remuneration, regardless of
whether such terms are in plain, intelligible language.</p>
<p>National law contains a list of standard contract terms that may be
unfair which lists some additional terms compared to the Annex to the
UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>NETHERLANDS</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
contract terms considered unfair in all circumstances (i.e. black list)
and a list of contract terms which may be considered as unfair (i.e. a
form of grey list). The list has been extended compared to the
UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>AUSTRIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a black
list and a grey list of standard contract terms considered unfair and
partially extends the assessment of unfairness to individually
negotiated contract terms.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>POLAND</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a list of
terms which are considered to be unfair in case of doubt (i.e. a form of
grey list) and which goes beyond the Annex to the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>PORTUGAL</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law has broadened the
scope of the unfairness assessment to contract terms relating to the
definition of the main subject matter of the contract and the adequacy
of the price or remuneration, regardless of whether such terms are in
plain, intelligible language.</p>
<p>National law contains a list of standard contract terms that are
strictly prohibited (i.e. a black list) and a list of contract terms
that are prohibited in certain circumstances (i.e. a form of grey
list).</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>ROMANIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains an
indicative list of terms considered unfair, which has been extended
compared to the Annex to the UCTD.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>SLOVENIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law extends the
unfairness assessment to contract terms relating to the main subject
matter of the contract and to the adequacy of the price or remuneration,
regardless of whether such terms are in plain, intelligible
language.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>SLOVAKIA</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law contains a black
list of contract terms that are unfair in all circumstances.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>FINLAND</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law has broadened the
scope of the unfairness assessment to individually negotiated contract
terms and to the adequacy of the price or remuneration, regardless of
whether such terms are in plain, intelligible language.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>SWEDEN</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law extends the
unfairness assessment to contract terms relating to the definition of
the main subject matter of the contract and to the adequacy of the price
or remuneration, regardless of whether such terms are in plain,
intelligible language, as well as to individually negotiated contract
terms.</p></td>
</tr>
<tr class="table">
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>UNITED KINGDOM</p></td>
<td class="table" data-valign="top"><p>National law does not go beyond
the minimum standard of the UCTD. However, the indicative list in the
Annex to the UCTD has been extended.</p></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
